     <p><b>Denmark</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/95/En-us-Denmark.ogg" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="11" data-file-height="11"></a><sup><span class="IPA" style="color:#00e;font:bold 80% sans-serif;padding:0 .1em"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Denmark.ogg" title="File:En-us-Denmark.ogg">i</a></span></sup></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɛ/ short 'e' in 'bed'">ɛ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɑːr/ 'ar' in 'bard'">ɑːr</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>: <span lang="da"><i>Danmark</i></span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Danish" title="Help:IPA for Danish">[ˈd̥ænmɑɡ̊]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&nbsp;(<a href="/wiki/File:DA-Danmark.ogg" title="File:DA-Danmark.ogg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500"></a> <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cc/DA-Danmark.ogg" class="internal" title="DA-Danmark.ogg">listen</a>)</small>) is a <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavian</a> country in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. The southernmost of the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic countries</a>, it is southwest of <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> and south of <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, and bordered to the south by <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>. The <b>Kingdom of Denmark</b><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[N 9]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> that comprises Denmark <a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/proper#Adjective" class="extiw" title="wikt:proper">proper</a><sup id="cite_ref-proper_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-proper-3">[N 2]</a></sup> and two autonomous <a href="/wiki/Constituent_country#Denmark" title="Constituent country">constituent countries</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic Ocean</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>. Denmark has an area of 42,924 <a href="/wiki/Square_kilometre" title="Square kilometre">square kilometres</a> (16,573&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-area_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-area-6">[2]</a></sup> and a population of 5,707,251 in January 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-pop1_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop1-7">[3]</a></sup> The country consists of a peninsula, <a href="/wiki/Jutland" title="Jutland">Jutland</a>, and an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> of <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Denmark" title="List of islands of Denmark">443 named islands</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[9]</a></sup> of which around 70 are inhabited. The islands are characterised by flat, <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable land</a> and sandy coasts, low elevation and a <a href="/wiki/Temperate" title="Temperate" class="mw-redirect">temperate</a> climate.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/History_of_Denmark" title="History of Denmark">unified kingdom of Denmark</a> emerged in the 8th century as a proficient seafaring nation in the struggle for <a href="/wiki/Dominium_maris_baltici" title="Dominium maris baltici">control of the Baltic Sea</a>. Danish monarchs ruled the personal <a href="/wiki/Kalmar_Union" title="Kalmar Union">Kalmar Union</a>, established in 1397 (of Denmark, Norway and Sweden), which ended with Swedish secession in 1523. Denmark and Norway remained under the same king until the union was dissolved by outside forces in 1814. Caused by the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a>, the deterioration of the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Empire" title="Norwegian Empire">Kingdom of Norway</a> made it possible for Denmark to inherit an <a href="/wiki/Danish_colonial_empire" title="Danish colonial empire">expansive colonial empire</a> from this union, of which the Faroe Islands and Greenland are remnants. Beginning in the 17th century, there were several <a href="/wiki/Cession" title="Cession">cessions</a> of territory; these culminated in the 1830s with a surge of <a href="/wiki/History_of_Denmark#The_19th_century" title="History of Denmark">nationalist movements</a>, which were defeated in the 1864 <a href="/wiki/Second_Schleswig_War" title="Second Schleswig War">Second Schleswig War</a>. Denmark remained neutral during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. In April 1940, a <a href="/wiki/German_invasion_of_Denmark_(1940)" title="German invasion of Denmark (1940)">German invasion</a> saw brief military skirmishes while the <a href="/wiki/Danish_resistance_movement" title="Danish resistance movement">Danish resistance movement</a> was active from 1943 until the <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Denmark#Hardship_and_the_end_of_the_war" title="Occupation of Denmark" class="mw-redirect">German surrender</a> in May 1945. An industrialized exporter of agricultural produce in the second half of the 19th century, Denmark introduced <a href="/wiki/Kanslergade_Agreement" title="Kanslergade Agreement">social and labour-market reforms</a> in the early 20th century that created the basis for the present <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">welfare state</a> <a href="/wiki/Nordic_model" title="Nordic model">model</a> with a highly developed <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a>.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Denmark" title="Constitution of Denmark">Constitution of Denmark</a> was signed on 5 June 1849, ending the <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a> which had begun in 1660. It establishes a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>—the current <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Denmark" title="Monarchy of Denmark">monarch</a> is <a href="/wiki/Margrethe_II_of_Denmark" title="Margrethe II of Denmark">Queen Margrethe II</a>—organised as a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> democracy. The <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Denmark" title="Politics of Denmark">government</a> and <a href="/wiki/Folketing" title="Folketing">national parliament</a> are seated in <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, the nation's <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Denmark_by_population" title="List of cities in Denmark by population">largest city</a> and main commercial centre. Denmark exercises <a href="/wiki/Hegemony" title="Hegemony">hegemonic</a> influence in the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Realm" title="Danish Realm">Danish Realm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">devolving</a> powers to handle internal affairs. Denmark became a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> in 1973, maintaining <a href="/wiki/Opt-outs_in_the_European_Union" title="Opt-outs in the European Union">certain opt-outs</a>; it retains its own currency, the <a href="/wiki/Danish_krone" title="Danish krone">krone</a>. It is among the founding members of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Council" title="Nordic Council">Nordic Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>; it is also part of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>.</p> 
     <p>Danes enjoy a high <a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">standard of living</a> and the country ranks highly in some metrics of national performance, including <a href="/wiki/Education_Index" title="Education Index">education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Health_care_in_Denmark" title="Health care in Denmark" class="mw-redirect">health care</a>, protection of <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">civil liberties</a>, <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">democratic governance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legatum_Prosperity_Index" title="Legatum Prosperity Index">prosperity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">human development</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Democracy_Index_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Democracy_Index-19">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[12]</a></sup> The country ranks as having the world's highest <a href="/wiki/Social_mobility" title="Social mobility">social mobility</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[13]</a></sup> a high level of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_income_equality" title="List of countries by income equality">income equality</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[14]</a></sup> has one of the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">highest per capita incomes</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">least corrupt country in the world</a>, and has one of the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_tax_rates" title="List of countries by tax rates">highest personal income tax rates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-taxation1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taxation1-24">[15]</a></sup> A large majority of Danes are members of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Denmark" title="Church of Denmark">National Church</a>, though the Constitution guarantees <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a>.</p> 
     <p></p>

         <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">8.7</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a></li> 
        </ul> </li> 
       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li> 
       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li> 
       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li> 
       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li> 
      </ul> 
     </div> 
     <p></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Etymology_of_Denmark" title="Etymology of Denmark">Etymology of Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The etymology of the word Denmark, and especially the relationship between Danes and Denmark and the unifying of Denmark as a single kingdom, is a subject which attracts debate.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[17]</a></sup> This is centred primarily on the prefix <i>"Dan"</i> and whether it refers to the <a href="/wiki/Danes_(Germanic_tribe)" title="Danes (Germanic tribe)">Dani</a> or a historical person <a href="/wiki/Dan_(king)" title="Dan (king)">Dan</a> and the exact meaning of the -<i>"mark"</i> ending.</p> 
     <p>Most handbooks derive the first part of the word, and the name of the people, from a word meaning "flat land",<sup id="cite_ref-et1_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-et1-27">[18]</a></sup> related to German <i>Tenne</i> "threshing floor", English <i>den</i> "cave".<sup id="cite_ref-et1_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-et1-27">[18]</a></sup> The <i>-mark</i> is believed to mean woodland or borderland (see <a href="/wiki/March_(territory)" title="March (territory)" class="mw-redirect">marches</a>), with probable references to the border forests in south <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Schleswig" title="Duchy of Schleswig">Schleswig</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[19]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The first recorded use of the word <i>Danmark</i> within Denmark itself is found on the two <a href="/wiki/Jelling_stones" title="Jelling stones">Jelling stones</a>, which are <a href="/wiki/Runestone" title="Runestone">runestones</a> believed to have been erected by <a href="/wiki/Gorm_the_Old" title="Gorm the Old">Gorm the Old</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 955</span>) and <a href="/wiki/Harald_Bluetooth" title="Harald Bluetooth">Harald Bluetooth</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 965</span>). The larger stone of the two is popularly cited as Denmark's baptismal certificate (<i>dåbsattest</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[20]</a></sup> though both use the word "Denmark", in the form of <a href="/wiki/Accusative_case" title="Accusative case">accusative</a> <span title="runes" class="script-runic" lang="gem-Runr" style="font-family: 'Segoe UI Historic', 'Segoe UI Symbol', Junicode, 'Free Monospaced', Code2000, Hnias, 'Noto Sans Runic';">ᛏᛅᚾᛘᛅᚢᚱᚴ</span> "tanmaurk" (<span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[danmɒrk]</span>) on the large stone, and <a href="/wiki/Genitive_case" title="Genitive case">genitive</a> <span title="runes" class="script-runic" lang="gem-Runr" style="font-family: 'Segoe UI Historic', 'Segoe UI Symbol', Junicode, 'Free Monospaced', Code2000, Hnias, 'Noto Sans Runic';">ᛏᛅᚾᛘᛅᚱᚴᛅᚱ</span> "tanmarkar" (pronounced <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[danmarkaɽ]</span>) on the small stone.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[21]</a></sup> The inhabitants of Denmark are there called "tani" (<span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[danɪ]</span>), or "Danes", in the accusative.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Denmark" title="History of Denmark">History of Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Greenland" title="History of Greenland">History of Greenland</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="History of the Faroe Islands">History of the Faroe Islands</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Solvognen_DO-6865_2000.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Solvognen_DO-6865_2000.jpg/220px-Solvognen_DO-6865_2000.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Solvognen_DO-6865_2000.jpg/330px-Solvognen_DO-6865_2000.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Solvognen_DO-6865_2000.jpg/440px-Solvognen_DO-6865_2000.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1438"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Solvognen_DO-6865_2000.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The gilded side of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Trundholm_sun_chariot" title="Trundholm sun chariot">Trundholm sun chariot</a> dating from the Nordic Bronze Age.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The earliest <a href="/wiki/Archaeology_of_Denmark" title="Archaeology of Denmark">archaeological findings in Denmark</a> date back to the <a href="/wiki/Eemian" title="Eemian">Eem interglacial period</a> from 130,000–110,000 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[22]</a></sup> Denmark has been inhabited since around 12,500 BC and agriculture has been evident since 3900 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-foreign_ministry_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foreign_ministry-32">[23]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Bronze_Age" title="Nordic Bronze Age">Nordic Bronze Age</a> (1800–600 BC) in Denmark was marked by <a href="/wiki/Tumulus" title="Tumulus">burial mounds</a>, which left an abundance of findings including <a href="/wiki/Lur" title="Lur">lurs</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Trundholm_sun_chariot" title="Trundholm sun chariot">Sun Chariot</a>.</p> 
     <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_Iron_Age" title="Pre-Roman Iron Age" class="mw-redirect">Pre-Roman Iron Age</a> (500 BC&nbsp;– AD 1), native groups began migrating south, and the first tribal <a href="/wiki/Danes_(Germanic_tribe)" title="Danes (Germanic tribe)">Danes</a> came to the country between the Pre-Roman and the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_Iron_Age" title="Germanic Iron Age">Germanic Iron Age</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[24]</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Iron_Age" title="Roman Iron Age" class="mw-redirect">Roman Iron Age</a> (AD 1–400).<sup id="cite_ref-foreign_ministry_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foreign_ministry-32">[23]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">Roman provinces</a> maintained <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">trade routes</a> and relations with native tribes in Denmark, and <a href="/wiki/Roman_currency" title="Roman currency">Roman coins</a> have been found in Denmark. Evidence of strong Celtic cultural influence dates from this period in Denmark and much of North-West Europe and is among other things reflected in the finding of the <a href="/wiki/Gundestrup_cauldron" title="Gundestrup cauldron">Gundestrup cauldron</a>.</p> 
     <p>The tribal Danes came from the east <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Denmark" title="List of islands of Denmark">Danish islands</a> (<a href="/wiki/Zealand" title="Zealand">Zealand</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Scania" title="Scania">Scania</a> and spoke an early form of <a href="/wiki/North_Germanic_languages" title="North Germanic languages">North Germanic</a>. Historians believe that before their arrival, most of <a href="/wiki/Jutland" title="Jutland">Jutland</a> and the nearest islands were settled by tribal <a href="/wiki/Jutes" title="Jutes">Jutes</a>. The Jutes migrated to Great Britain eventually, some as mercenaries by <a href="/wiki/Brythonic_languages" title="Brythonic languages" class="mw-redirect">Brythonic</a> King <a href="/wiki/Vortigern" title="Vortigern">Vortigern</a>, and were granted the south-eastern territories of <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a> and other areas, where they settled. They were later absorbed or <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnically cleansed</a> by the invading <a href="/wiki/Angles" title="Angles">Angles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a>, who formed the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxons</a>. The remaining Jutish population in Jutland assimilated in with the settling <a href="/wiki/Danes_(Germanic_tribe)" title="Danes (Germanic tribe)">Danes</a>.</p> 
     <p>A short note about the <i>Dani</i> in "<a href="/wiki/Getica" title="Getica">Getica</a>" by the historian <a href="/wiki/Jordanes" title="Jordanes">Jordanes</a> is believed to be an early mention of the Danes, one of the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic groups</a> from whom modern <a href="/wiki/Danes" title="Danes">Danes</a> are descended.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[26]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Danevirke" title="Danevirke">Danevirke</a> defence structures were built in phases from the 3rd century forward and the sheer size of the construction efforts in AD 737 are attributed to the emergence of a Danish king.<sup id="cite_ref-danevirke_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-danevirke-36">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-danevirke_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-danevirke-36">[27]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Younger_Futhark" title="Younger Futhark">new runic alphabet</a> was first used around the same time and <a href="/wiki/Ribe" title="Ribe">Ribe</a>, the oldest town of Denmark, was founded about AD 700.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Viking_and_Middle_Ages">Viking and Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Viking and Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Viking_Age" title="Viking Age">Viking Age</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Kalmar_Union" title="Kalmar Union">Kalmar Union</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ladbyskibet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Ladbyskibet.jpg/220px-Ladbyskibet.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Ladbyskibet.jpg/330px-Ladbyskibet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Ladbyskibet.jpg/440px-Ladbyskibet.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="568"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Ladbyskibet.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Ladby_ship" title="Ladby ship">Ladby ship</a>, the largest ship burial found in Denmark.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>From the 8th to the 10th century Denmark, and the wider Scandinavian region, was the source of <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Vikings</a>. They colonised, raided, and traded in all parts of Europe. Viking explorers first discovered <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> by accident in the 9th century when heading for the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a>, and Norwegian Vikings eventually came across "<a href="/wiki/Vinland" title="Vinland">Vinland</a>", known today as <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. The Danish Vikings were most active in the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a> and Western Europe. They conquered and settled parts of England (known as the <a href="/wiki/Danelaw" title="Danelaw">Danelaw</a>) under King <a href="/wiki/Sweyn_Forkbeard" title="Sweyn Forkbeard">Sweyn Forkbeard</a> in 1013, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, and France where Danes and Norwegians founded <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a> with <a href="/wiki/Rollo" title="Rollo">Rollo</a> as head of state. More <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxon</a> <a href="/wiki/Pence" title="Pence" class="mw-redirect">pence</a> of this period have been found in Denmark than in England.<sup id="cite_ref-Lund_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lund-37">[28]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Jellingsten_stor_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Large stone containing a carved depiction of Jesus Christ" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Jellingsten_stor_1.jpg/170px-Jellingsten_stor_1.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Jellingsten_stor_1.jpg/255px-Jellingsten_stor_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Jellingsten_stor_1.jpg/340px-Jellingsten_stor_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="800"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Jellingsten_stor_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Larger of the two Jelling stones, raised by 
        <a href="/wiki/Harald_Bluetooth" title="Harald Bluetooth">Harald Bluetooth</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>As attested by the <a href="/wiki/Jelling_stones" title="Jelling stones">Jelling stones</a>, the Danes were united and <a href="/wiki/Christianised" title="Christianised" class="mw-redirect">Christianised</a> about 965 by <a href="/wiki/Harald_Bluetooth" title="Harald Bluetooth">Harald Bluetooth</a>. It is believed that Denmark became Christian for political reasons so as not to get invaded by the rising <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Christian power</a> in Europe, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, which was an important trading area for the Danes. In that case Harald built six <a href="/wiki/Fortresses" title="Fortresses" class="mw-redirect">fortresses</a> around Denmark called <a href="/wiki/Viking_ring_fortress" title="Viking ring fortress">Trelleborg</a> and built a further <a href="/wiki/Danevirke" title="Danevirke">Danevirke</a>. In the early 11th century, <a href="/wiki/Canute_the_Great" title="Canute the Great" class="mw-redirect">Canute the Great</a> won and united Denmark, England, and Norway for almost 30 years with a Scandinavian army.<sup id="cite_ref-Lund_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lund-37">[28]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Throughout the <a href="/wiki/High_Middle_Ages" title="High Middle Ages">High</a> and <a href="/wiki/Late_Middle_Ages" title="Late Middle Ages">Late Middle Ages</a>, Denmark also included <a href="/wiki/Sk%C3%A5neland" title="Skåneland">Skåneland</a> (the areas of Scania, <a href="/wiki/Halland" title="Halland">Halland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Blekinge" title="Blekinge">Blekinge</a> in present-day south Sweden) and Danish kings ruled <a href="/wiki/Danish_Estonia" title="Danish Estonia">Danish Estonia</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Duchy" title="Duchy">duchies</a> of <a href="/wiki/Schleswig" title="Schleswig" class="mw-redirect">Schleswig</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holstein" title="Holstein">Holstein</a>. Most of the latter two now form the state of <a href="/wiki/Schleswig-Holstein" title="Schleswig-Holstein">Schleswig-Holstein</a> in northern Germany.</p> 
     <p>In 1397, Denmark entered into a <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> with <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweden%E2%80%93Finland" title="Sweden–Finland">Sweden</a>, united under Queen <a href="/wiki/Margaret_I_of_Denmark" title="Margaret I of Denmark">Margaret I</a>. The three countries were to be treated as equals in the union. However, even from the start Margaret may not have been so idealistic—treating Denmark as the clear "senior" partner of the union.<sup id="cite_ref-Lauring_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lauring-38">[29]</a></sup> Thus, much of the next 125 years of <a href="/wiki/History_of_Scandinavia" title="History of Scandinavia">Scandinavian history</a> revolves around this union, with Sweden breaking off and being re-conquered repeatedly. The issue was for practical purposes resolved on 17 June 1523, as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Swedish_monarchs" title="List of Swedish monarchs">Swedish King</a> <a href="/wiki/Gustav_I_of_Sweden" title="Gustav I of Sweden">Gustav Vasa</a> conquered the city of <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a> spread to Scandinavia in the 1530s, and following the <a href="/wiki/Count%27s_Feud" title="Count's Feud">Count's Feud</a> civil war, <a href="/wiki/Reformation_in_Denmark%E2%80%93Norway_and_Holstein" title="Reformation in Denmark–Norway and Holstein">Denmark converted</a> to <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a> in 1536. Later that year, Denmark entered into a union with Norway.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_history_.281536.E2.80.931849.29">Early modern history (1536–1849)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early modern history (1536–1849)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Norway" title="Denmark–Norway">Denmark–Norway</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Danish_colonial_empire" title="Danish colonial empire">Danish colonial empire</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Carta_Marina_-_Dannevirke.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Carta_Marina_-_Dannevirke.jpeg/220px-Carta_Marina_-_Dannevirke.jpeg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Carta_Marina_-_Dannevirke.jpeg/330px-Carta_Marina_-_Dannevirke.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Carta_Marina_-_Dannevirke.jpeg/440px-Carta_Marina_-_Dannevirke.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="800"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Carta_Marina_-_Dannevirke.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Portion of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Carta_marina" title="Carta marina">Carta marina</a>, an early map of Scandinavia, made around the start of the union with Norway.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>After Sweden permanently <a href="/wiki/Foundation_of_modern_Sweden" title="Foundation of modern Sweden" class="mw-redirect">broke away</a> from the personal union, Denmark tried on several occasions to reassert control over its neighbour. King <a href="/wiki/Christian_IV_of_Denmark" title="Christian IV of Denmark">Christian IV</a> attacked Sweden in the 1611–1613 <a href="/wiki/Kalmar_War" title="Kalmar War">Kalmar War</a> but failed to accomplish his main objective of forcing it to return to the union. The war led to no territorial changes, but Sweden was forced to pay a <a href="/wiki/War_reparations" title="War reparations">war indemnity</a> of 1 million silver <a href="/wiki/Riksdaler" title="Riksdaler" class="mw-redirect">riksdaler</a> to Denmark, an amount known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Stettin_(1570)" title="Treaty of Stettin (1570)">Älvsborg ransom</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[30]</a></sup> King Christian used this money to found several towns and fortresses, most notably <a href="/wiki/Gl%C3%BCckstadt" title="Glückstadt">Glückstadt</a> (founded as a rival to <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Christiania</a>. Inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a>, he founded a similar <a href="/wiki/Danish_East_India_Company" title="Danish East India Company">Danish company</a> and planned to claim <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Ceylon</a> as a colony, but the company only managed to acquire <a href="/wiki/Tharangambadi" title="Tharangambadi">Tranquebar</a> on India's <a href="/wiki/Coromandel_Coast" title="Coromandel Coast">Coromandel Coast</a>. Denmark's large colonial aspirations were limited to a few key <a href="/wiki/Trading_posts" title="Trading posts" class="mw-redirect">trading posts</a> in Africa and India. The empire was sustained by trade with other major powers, and <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">plantations</a> – ultimately a lack of resources led to its stagnation.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[31]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>, Christian tried to become the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a> states in Germany but suffered a crushing defeat at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lutter" title="Battle of Lutter">Battle of Lutter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[32]</a></sup> The result was that the Catholic army under <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_von_Wallenstein" title="Albrecht von Wallenstein">Albrecht von Wallenstein</a> was able to invade, occupy, and pillage Jutland, forcing Denmark <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_L%C3%BCbeck" title="Treaty of Lübeck">to withdraw from the war</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[33]</a></sup> Denmark managed to avoid territorial concessions, but King <a href="/wiki/Gustavus_Adolphus_of_Sweden" title="Gustavus Adolphus of Sweden">Gustavus Adolphus</a>' intervention in Germany was seen as a sign that the military power of Sweden was on the rise while Denmark's influence in the region was declining. In 1643, Swedish armies <a href="/wiki/Torstenson_War" title="Torstenson War">invaded Jutland</a> and claimed Scania in 1644.</p> 
     <p>In the 1645 <a href="/wiki/Second_Treaty_of_Br%C3%B6msebro_(1645)" title="Second Treaty of Brömsebro (1645)">Treaty of Brømsebro</a>, Denmark surrendered Halland, <a href="/wiki/Gotland" title="Gotland">Gotland</a>, the last parts of Danish Estonia, and several provinces in Norway. In 1657, King <a href="/wiki/Frederick_III_of_Denmark" title="Frederick III of Denmark">Frederick III</a> declared war on Sweden and marched on <a href="/wiki/Bremen-Verden" title="Bremen-Verden">Bremen-Verden</a>. This led to a massive Danish defeat and the armies of King <a href="/wiki/Charles_X_Gustav" title="Charles X Gustav" class="mw-redirect">Charles X Gustav</a> of Sweden conquered both <a href="/wiki/Jutland" title="Jutland">Jutland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Funen" title="Funen">Funen</a>, and much of <a href="/wiki/Zealand" title="Zealand">Zealand</a> before signing the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Roskilde" title="Treaty of Roskilde">Peace of Roskilde</a> in February 1658 which gave Sweden control of Scania, <a href="/wiki/Blekinge" title="Blekinge">Blekinge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tr%C3%B8ndelag" title="Trøndelag">Trøndelag</a>, and the island of <a href="/wiki/Bornholm" title="Bornholm">Bornholm</a>. Charles X Gustav quickly regretted not having destroyed Denmark completely and in August 1658 he began a two-year-long siege of <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> but failed to take the capital. In the following peace settlement, Denmark managed to maintain its independence and regain control of Trøndelag and Bornholm.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Slaget_vid_%C3%96land_Claus_M%C3%B8inichen_1686.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Slaget_vid_%C3%96land_Claus_M%C3%B8inichen_1686.jpg/280px-Slaget_vid_%C3%96land_Claus_M%C3%B8inichen_1686.jpg" width="280" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Slaget_vid_%C3%96land_Claus_M%C3%B8inichen_1686.jpg/420px-Slaget_vid_%C3%96land_Claus_M%C3%B8inichen_1686.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Slaget_vid_%C3%96land_Claus_M%C3%B8inichen_1686.jpg/560px-Slaget_vid_%C3%96land_Claus_M%C3%B8inichen_1686.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="508"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Slaget_vid_%C3%96land_Claus_M%C3%B8inichen_1686.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_%C3%96land" title="Battle of Öland">Battle of Öland</a> during the Scanian War, between an allied 
        <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Norway" title="Denmark–Norway">Dano-Norwegian</a>-
        <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch</a> fleet and the Swedish navy, 1 June 1676.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Denmark tried to regain control of Scania in the <a href="/wiki/Scanian_War" title="Scanian War">Scanian War</a> (1675-1679) but it ended in failure. Following the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War" title="Great Northern War">Great Northern War</a> (1700–21), Denmark managed to restore control of the parts of <a href="/wiki/Schleswig" title="Schleswig" class="mw-redirect">Schleswig</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holstein" title="Holstein">Holstein</a> ruled by the house of <a href="/wiki/Holstein-Gottorp" title="Holstein-Gottorp" class="mw-redirect">Holstein-Gottorp</a> in 1721 and 1773, respectively. Denmark prospered greatly in the last decades of the eighteenth century due to its <a href="/wiki/Country_neutrality_(international_relations)" title="Country neutrality (international relations)">neutral status</a> allowing it to trade with both sides in the many contemporary wars. In the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, Denmark traded with both <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">France</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a> and joined the <a href="/wiki/Second_League_of_Armed_Neutrality" title="Second League of Armed Neutrality">League of Armed Neutrality</a> with <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a>, Sweden, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[34]</a></sup> The British considered this a hostile act and attacked Copenhagen in both <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Copenhagen_(1801)" title="Battle of Copenhagen (1801)">1801</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Copenhagen_(1807)" title="Battle of Copenhagen (1807)">1807</a>, in one case carrying off the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Danish_Navy" title="Royal Danish Navy">Danish fleet</a>, in the other, burning large parts of the Danish capital. This led to the so-called Danish-British <a href="/wiki/Gunboat_War" title="Gunboat War">Gunboat War</a>. British control over the waterways between Denmark and Norway proved disastrous to the union's economy and in 1813 Denmark–Norway went <a href="/wiki/Bankruptcy" title="Bankruptcy">bankrupt</a>.</p> 
     <p>The Danish-Norwegian union was dissolved by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Kiel" title="Treaty of Kiel">Treaty of Kiel</a> in 1814; the Danish monarchy "irrevocably and forever" renounced claims to the Kingdom of Norway in favour of the Swedish king.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[35]</a></sup> After the dissolution of the union with Norway, Denmark kept the possessions of <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> (which retained the Danish monarchy until 1944), the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, all of which had been governed by Norway for centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[36]</a></sup> Apart from the Nordic colonies, Denmark continued to rule over <a href="/wiki/Danish_India" title="Danish India">Danish India</a> from 1620 to 1869, the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Gold_Coast" title="Danish Gold Coast">Danish Gold Coast</a> (Ghana) from 1658 to 1850, and the <a href="/wiki/Danish_West_Indies" title="Danish West Indies">Danish West Indies</a> from 1671 to 1917.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitutional_monarchy_.281849.E2.80.93present.29">Constitutional monarchy (1849–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Constitutional monarchy (1849–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Grundlovgivende_rigsforsamling_-_Constantin_Hansen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Grundlovgivende_rigsforsamling_-_Constantin_Hansen.jpg/220px-Grundlovgivende_rigsforsamling_-_Constantin_Hansen.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Grundlovgivende_rigsforsamling_-_Constantin_Hansen.jpg/330px-Grundlovgivende_rigsforsamling_-_Constantin_Hansen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Grundlovgivende_rigsforsamling_-_Constantin_Hansen.jpg/440px-Grundlovgivende_rigsforsamling_-_Constantin_Hansen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="686"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Grundlovgivende_rigsforsamling_-_Constantin_Hansen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <i>Den Grundlovsgivende Rigsforsamling</i> – The Constitutional Assembly of the Realm was assembled by King 
        <a href="/wiki/Frederick_VII_of_Denmark" title="Frederick VII of Denmark">Frederick VII</a> in 1848 to adopt the 
        <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Denmark" title="Constitution of Denmark">Constitution of Denmark</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>A nascent Danish liberal and national movement gained momentum in the 1830s; after the European <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848" title="Revolutions of 1848">Revolutions of 1848</a>, Denmark peacefully became a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> on 5 June 1849. A <a href="/wiki/Rigsdagen" title="Rigsdagen">two-chamber parliament</a> was established. Denmark faced war against both <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Austria" title="Habsburg Austria" class="mw-redirect">Habsburg Austria</a> in what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Second_Schleswig_War" title="Second Schleswig War">Second Schleswig War</a>, lasting from February to October 1864. Denmark was defeated and obliged to <a href="/wiki/Cession" title="Cession">cede</a> <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Schleswig-Holstein" title="Province of Schleswig-Holstein">Schleswig and Holstein</a> to <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>. This loss came as the latest in the long series of defeats and territorial loss that had begun in the 17th century. After these events, Denmark pursued a policy of neutrality in Europe.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Industrialization" title="Industrialization" class="mw-redirect">Industrialization</a> came to Denmark in the second half of the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[37]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/History_of_rail_transport_in_Denmark" title="History of rail transport in Denmark">nation's first railroads</a> were constructed in the 1850s, and improved communications and overseas trade allowed industry to develop in spite of Denmark's lack of natural resources. <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">Trade unions</a> developed starting in the 1870s. There was a considerable migration of people from the countryside to the cities, and Danish agriculture became centred on the export of dairy and meat products.</p> 
     <p>Denmark maintained its neutral stance during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. After the defeat of Germany, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Versailles powers</a> offered to return the region of Schleswig-Holstein to Denmark. Fearing German <a href="/wiki/Irredentism" title="Irredentism">irredentism</a>, Denmark refused to consider the return of the area without a <a href="/wiki/Plebiscite" title="Plebiscite" class="mw-redirect">plebiscite</a>; the two <a href="/wiki/Schleswig_Plebiscites" title="Schleswig Plebiscites" class="mw-redirect">Schleswig Plebiscites</a> took place on 10 February and 14 March 1920, respectively. On 10 July 1920, Northern Schleswig was recovered by Denmark, thereby adding some 163,600 inhabitants and 3,984 square kilometres (1,538&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi).</p> 
     <p>In 1939 Denmark signed a 10-year non-aggression pact with <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> but <a href="/wiki/Operation_Weser%C3%BCbung" title="Operation Weserübung">Germany invaded Denmark</a> on 9 April 1940 and the Danish government quickly surrendered. <a href="/wiki/Denmark_in_World_War_II" title="Denmark in World War II">World War II in Denmark</a> was characterized by economic co-operation with Germany until 1943, when the Danish government refused further co-operation and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Danish_Navy" title="Royal Danish Navy">its navy</a> scuttled most of its ships and sent many of its officers to Sweden, which was neutral. The <a href="/wiki/Danish_resistance_movement" title="Danish resistance movement">Danish resistance</a> performed a <a href="/wiki/Rescue_of_the_Danish_Jews" title="Rescue of the Danish Jews">rescue operation</a> that managed to evacuate several thousand <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Denmark" title="History of the Jews in Denmark">Jews</a> and their families to safety in Sweden before the Germans could send them to death camps. Some Danes supported <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a> by joining the <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_Workers%27_Party_of_Denmark" title="National Socialist Workers' Party of Denmark">Danish Nazi Party</a> or volunteering to fight with Germany as part of the <a href="/wiki/Frikorps_Danmark" title="Frikorps Danmark" class="mw-redirect">Frikorps Danmark</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[38]</a></sup> Iceland severed ties to Denmark and <a href="/wiki/Founding_of_the_republic_of_Iceland" title="Founding of the republic of Iceland" class="mw-redirect">became an independent republic</a> in 1944; <a href="/wiki/Liberation_of_Denmark" title="Liberation of Denmark" class="mw-redirect">Germany surrendered</a> in May 1945; in 1948, the Faroe Islands gained <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">home rule</a>; in 1949, Denmark became a founding member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/220px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/330px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/440px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="521" data-file-height="310"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Denmark became a member of the European Union in 1973 and signed the 
        <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Treaty" title="Lisbon Treaty" class="mw-redirect">Lisbon Treaty</a> in 2007.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Denmark was a founding member of <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">European Free Trade Association</a> (EFTA). During the 1960s, the EFTA countries were often referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Seven" title="Outer Seven" class="mw-redirect">Outer Seven</a>, as opposed to the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Six" title="Inner Six">Inner Six</a> of what was then the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC).<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[39]</a></sup> In 1973, along with Britain and Ireland, Denmark joined the European Economic Community (now the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>) after a <a href="/wiki/Danish_European_Communities_membership_referendum,_1972" title="Danish European Communities membership referendum, 1972">public referendum</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a>, which involved further European integration, <a href="/wiki/Danish_Maastricht_Treaty_referendum,_1992" title="Danish Maastricht Treaty referendum, 1992">was rejected</a> by the Danish people in 1992; it was only accepted after a <a href="/wiki/Danish_Maastricht_Treaty_referendum,_1993" title="Danish Maastricht Treaty referendum, 1993">second referendum</a> in 1993, which provided for <a href="/wiki/Opt-outs_in_the_European_Union" title="Opt-outs in the European Union">four opt-outs</a> from policies. The Danes rejected the euro as the national currency in <a href="/wiki/Danish_euro_referendum,_2000" title="Danish euro referendum, 2000">a referendum in 2000</a>. Greenland gained home rule in 1979 and was awarded <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">self-determination</a> in 2009. Neither the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands_and_the_European_Union" title="Faroe Islands and the European Union">Faroe Islands</a> nor <a href="/wiki/Greenland%E2%80%93European_Union_relations#Outside_the_EU" title="Greenland–European Union relations">Greenland</a> are members of the Union, the Faroese having declined membership of the EEC in 1973 and Greenland in 1986, in both cases because of fisheries policies.</p> 
     <p>Constitutional change in 1953 led to a <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">single-chamber</a> parliament elected by proportional representation, female accession to the Danish throne, and Greenland becoming an integral part of Denmark. The <a href="/wiki/Centre-left" title="Centre-left" class="mw-redirect">centre-left</a> <a href="/wiki/Social_Democrats_(Denmark)" title="Social Democrats (Denmark)">Social Democrats</a> led a string of coalition governments for most of the second half of the 20th century in a country generally known for its liberal traditions. The <a href="/wiki/Venstre_(Denmark)" title="Venstre (Denmark)">Liberal Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_People%27s_Party_(Denmark)" title="Conservative People's Party (Denmark)">Conservative People's Party</a> have also led <a href="/wiki/Centre-right" title="Centre-right" class="mw-redirect">centre-right</a> governments. In recent years the <a href="/wiki/Danish_People%27s_Party" title="Danish People's Party">Danish People's Party</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_populist" title="Right-wing populist" class="mw-redirect">right-wing populist</a> party,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[40]</a></sup> has emerged as a major party—becoming the second-largest following the <a href="/wiki/Danish_general_election,_2015" title="Danish general election, 2015">2015 general election</a>—during which time immigration and integration have become major issues of public debate.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Denmark" title="Geography of Denmark">Geography of Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      Also related: 
      <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Geography of the Faroe Islands">Geography of the Faroe Islands</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Greenland" title="Geography of Greenland">Geography of Greenland</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_image_of_Denmark_in_July_2001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Satellite image" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Satellite_image_of_Denmark_in_July_2001.jpg/220px-Satellite_image_of_Denmark_in_July_2001.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Satellite_image_of_Denmark_in_July_2001.jpg/330px-Satellite_image_of_Denmark_in_July_2001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Satellite_image_of_Denmark_in_July_2001.jpg/440px-Satellite_image_of_Denmark_in_July_2001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1905" data-file-height="1420"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_image_of_Denmark_in_July_2001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> A satellite image of Jutland and the Danish islands.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Located in Northern Europe, Denmark<sup id="cite_ref-proper_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-proper-3">[N 2]</a></sup> consists of the peninsula of <a href="/wiki/Jutland" title="Jutland">Jutland</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Denmark" title="List of islands of Denmark">443 named islands</a> (1,419 islands above 100 square metres (1,100&nbsp;sq&nbsp;ft) in total).<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[42]</a></sup> Of these, 74 are inhabited (January 2015),<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[43]</a></sup> with the largest being <a href="/wiki/Zealand" title="Zealand">Zealand</a>, the <a href="/wiki/North_Jutlandic_Island" title="North Jutlandic Island">North Jutlandic Island</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Funen" title="Funen">Funen</a>. The island of <a href="/wiki/Bornholm" title="Bornholm">Bornholm</a> is located east of the rest of the country, in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>. Many of the larger islands are connected by bridges; the <a href="/wiki/%C3%98resund_Bridge" title="Øresund Bridge">Øresund Bridge</a> connects Zealand with Sweden; the <a href="/wiki/Great_Belt_Fixed_Link" title="Great Belt Fixed Link">Great Belt Bridge</a> connects Funen with Zealand; and the <a href="/wiki/Little_Belt_Bridge_(1970)" title="Little Belt Bridge (1970)">Little Belt Bridge</a> connects Jutland with Funen. <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">Ferries</a> or <a href="/wiki/Small_aircraft" title="Small aircraft" class="mw-redirect">small aircraft</a> connect to the smaller islands. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Denmark_by_population" title="List of cities in Denmark by population">largest cities</a> with populations over 100,000 are the capital <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> on Zealand; <a href="/wiki/Aarhus" title="Aarhus">Aarhus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aalborg" title="Aalborg">Aalborg</a> in Jutland; and <a href="/wiki/Odense" title="Odense">Odense</a> on Funen.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Denmark_map.gif" class="image"><img alt="A labelled map of Denmark" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Denmark_map.gif/220px-Denmark_map.gif" width="220" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/35/Denmark_map.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/35/Denmark_map.gif 2x" data-file-width="326" data-file-height="350"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Denmark_map.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> A map showing 
        <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_in_Denmark_by_population" title="List of urban areas in Denmark by population">major urban areas</a>, highest and lowest natural points, and the larger islands.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The country occupies a total area of 42,924 <a href="/wiki/Square_kilometre" title="Square kilometre">square kilometres</a> (16,573&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi)<sup id="cite_ref-area_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-area-6">[2]</a></sup> The area of inland water is 700&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (270&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), variously stated as from 500 – 700&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (193-270 sq m). The size of the land area cannot be stated exactly since the ocean constantly erodes and adds material to the coastline, and because of human <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">land reclamation</a> projects (to counter erosion). <a href="/wiki/Post-glacial_rebound" title="Post-glacial rebound">Post-glacial rebound</a> raises the land by a bit less than 1&nbsp;cm (0.4&nbsp;in) per year in the north and east, extending the coast. A circle enclosing the same area as Denmark would be 234 kilometres (145 miles) in <a href="/wiki/Diameter" title="Diameter">diameter</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Circumference" title="Circumference">circumference</a> of 742&nbsp;km (461&nbsp;mi). It shares a border of 68 kilometres (42&nbsp;mi) with <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> to the south and is otherwise surrounded by 8,750&nbsp;km (5,437&nbsp;mi) of tidal <a href="/wiki/Shoreline" title="Shoreline" class="mw-redirect">shoreline</a> (including small <a href="/wiki/Bay" title="Bay">bays</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inlet" title="Inlet">inlets</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Nature_and_Environment_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nature_and_Environment-53">[44]</a></sup> No location in Denmark is further from the coast than 52&nbsp;km (32&nbsp;mi). On the south-west coast of Jutland, the tide is between 1 and 2&nbsp;m (3.28 and 6.56&nbsp;ft), and the tideline moves outward and inward on a 10&nbsp;km (6.2&nbsp;mi) stretch.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[45]</a></sup> Denmark's territorial waters total 105,000 square kilometres (40,541 square miles).</p> 
     <p>Denmark's northernmost point is <a href="/wiki/Skagen" title="Skagen">Skagen</a>'s point (the north beach of the Skaw) at 57° 45' 7" northern latitude; the southernmost is <a href="/wiki/Gedser" title="Gedser">Gedser</a> point (the southern tip of <a href="/wiki/Falster" title="Falster">Falster</a>) at 54° 33' 35" northern latitude; the westernmost point is <a href="/wiki/Bl%C3%A5vandshuk" title="Blåvandshuk">Blåvandshuk</a> at 8° 4' 22" eastern longitude; and the easternmost point is <a href="/wiki/%C3%98stersk%C3%A6r" title="Østerskær">Østerskær</a> at 15° 11' 55" eastern longitude. This is in the archipelago <a href="/wiki/Ertholmene" title="Ertholmene">Ertholmene</a> 18 kilometres (11&nbsp;mi) north-east of Bornholm. The distance from east to west is 452 kilometres (281&nbsp;mi), from north to south 368 kilometres (229&nbsp;mi).</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Denmark_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Denmark_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Denmark_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Denmark_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Denmark_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Denmark_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Denmark_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1395"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Denmark_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Denmark map of Köppen climate classification.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The country is flat with little elevation; having an average height <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level" class="mw-redirect">above sea level</a> of 31 metres (102&nbsp;ft). The highest natural point is <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B8lleh%C3%B8j" title="Møllehøj">Møllehøj</a>, at 170.86 metres (560.56&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[46]</a></sup> A sizeable portion of Denmark's <a href="/wiki/Terrain" title="Terrain">terrain</a> consists of rolling <a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">plains</a> whilst the coastline is sandy, with large <a href="/wiki/Dune" title="Dune">dunes</a> in northern Jutland. Although once extensively forested, today Denmark largely consists of <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable land</a>. It is drained by a <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Denmark" title="List of rivers of Denmark">dozen or so rivers</a>, and the most significant include the <a href="/wiki/Guden%C3%A5" title="Gudenå">Gudenå</a>, <a href="/wiki/Odense_River" title="Odense River">Odense</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skjern_River" title="Skjern River">Skjern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sus%C3%A5_River" title="Suså River">Suså</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vid%C3%A5" title="Vidå">Vidå</a>—a river that flows along its southern border with Germany.</p> 
     <p>The Kingdom of Denmark includes two overseas territories, both well to the west of Denmark: Greenland, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area" title="List of islands by area">world's largest island</a>, and the Faroe Islands in the North Atlantic Ocean. These territories are self-governing and form part of the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Realm" title="Danish Realm">Danish Realm</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>Denmark has a <a href="/wiki/Temperateness" title="Temperateness" class="mw-redirect">temperate</a> climate, characterised by mild winters, with mean temperatures in January of 1.5&nbsp;°C (34.7&nbsp;°F), and cool summers, with a mean temperature in August of 17.2&nbsp;°C (63.0&nbsp;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-Denmark_climate_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denmark_climate-56">[47]</a></sup> Denmark has an average of 179 days per year with precipitation, on average receiving a total of 765 millimetres (30&nbsp;in) per year; autumn is the wettest season and spring the driest.<sup id="cite_ref-Denmark_climate_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denmark_climate-56">[47]</a></sup> The position between a continent and an ocean means that weather often changes.<sup id="cite_ref-Denmark_weather_change_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denmark_weather_change-57">[48]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Because of Denmark's northern location, there are large seasonal variations in daylight. There are short days during the winter with sunrise coming around 8:45&nbsp;am and sunset 3:45&nbsp;pm (standard time), as well as long summer days with sunrise at 4:30&nbsp;am and sunset at 10&nbsp;pm (<a href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight saving time">daylight saving time</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-sunrise_sunset_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sunrise_sunset-58">[49]</a></sup></p> 
     <table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed" style="width:90%; text-align:center; font-size:90%; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity_and_environment">Biodiversity and environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Biodiversity and environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      Further information: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_forests_in_Denmark" title="List of forests in Denmark">List of forests in Denmark</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Denmark" title="List of mammals of Denmark">List of mammals of Denmark</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Denmark" title="List of birds of Denmark">List of birds of Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tmulti tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;max-width:452px"> 
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:186px;max-width:186px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Grib_skov.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Grib_skov.jpg/184px-Grib_skov.jpg" width="184" height="173" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Grib_skov.jpg/276px-Grib_skov.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Grib_skov.jpg/368px-Grib_skov.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1810" data-file-height="1700"></a>
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         <a href="/wiki/Fagus_sylvatica" title="Fagus sylvatica">Beech trees</a> are common throughout Denmark, especially in the sparse woodlands.
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:262px;max-width:262px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Baltic_sea_coast_of_skagen.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Baltic_sea_coast_of_skagen.JPG/260px-Baltic_sea_coast_of_skagen.JPG" width="260" height="173" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Baltic_sea_coast_of_skagen.JPG/390px-Baltic_sea_coast_of_skagen.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Baltic_sea_coast_of_skagen.JPG/520px-Baltic_sea_coast_of_skagen.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3722" data-file-height="2482"></a>
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         The Danish landscape is characterised by flat, 
         <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable land</a> and sandy coasts.
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <div style="clear:left"></div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Denmark belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a> and can be subdivided into two <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregions</a>: the Atlantic mixed forests and Baltic mixed forests.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[50]</a></sup> Most of Denmark's temperate forests have been substantially destroyed or fragmented, chiefly for agricultural uses over the last millennia. In all, 12.9% of the land is forested.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roe_deer" title="Roe deer">Roe deer</a> occupy the countryside in growing numbers, and large-antlered <a href="/wiki/Red_deer" title="Red deer">red deer</a> can be found in the sparse woodlands of Jutland. The country is also home to smaller mammals, such as <a href="/wiki/Hare" title="Hare">hares</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hedgehog" title="Hedgehog">hedgehogs</a>. Approximately 400 bird species inhabit Denmark and about 160 of those breed in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[52]</a></sup> Fish, particularly <a href="/wiki/Cod" title="Cod">cod</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herring" title="Herring">herring</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Plaice" title="Plaice">plaice</a>, are abundant in Danish waters and form the basis for a large fishing industry.</p> 
     <p>Land and water pollution are two of Denmark's most significant <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issue" title="Environmental issue">environmental issues</a> although much of country's household and industrial waste is now recycled. Denmark has historically taken a progressive stance on <a href="/wiki/Environmental_preservation" title="Environmental preservation" class="mw-redirect">environmental preservation</a>; in 1971 Denmark established a <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Environment_(Denmark)" title="Ministry of Environment (Denmark)">Ministry of Environment</a> and was the first country in the world to implement an <a href="/wiki/Environmental_law" title="Environmental law">environmental law</a> in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[53]</a></sup> To mitigate environmental degradation and <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> the Danish Government has signed the <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Climate Change-Kyoto Protocol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-63">[54]</a></sup> However, the national <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">ecological footprint</a> is 8.26 global hectares per person, which is very high compared to a world average of 1.7 in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[55]</a></sup> Contributing factors to this value are an exceptional high value for cropland but also a relatively high value for grazing land,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[56]</a></sup> which may be explained by the substantially high meat production in Denmark (115.8 kilograms (255&nbsp;lb) meat annually per capita) and the large economic role of the meat and dairy industries.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[57]</a></sup> In December 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Climate_Change_Performance_Index" title="Climate Change Performance Index">Climate Change Performance Index</a> for 2015 placed Denmark at the top of the table, explaining that although emissions are still quite high, the country was able to implement effective climate protection policies.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[58]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Denmark" title="Regions of Denmark">Regions of Denmark</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Denmark" title="Municipalities of Denmark">Municipalities of Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <div style="width: 250px; float: right; margin: none; padding: none; border: none; clear: right; background-color: #ffffff; position: relative;"> 
      <div style="background-color:&nbsp;;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Denmark_regions.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Denmark_regions.svg/250px-Denmark_regions.svg.png" width="250" height="300" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Denmark_regions.svg/375px-Denmark_regions.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Denmark_regions.svg/500px-Denmark_regions.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1656" data-file-height="1984"></a>
      </div>
