     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Denmark" title="Politics of Denmark">Politics of Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Politics of the Faroe Islands">Politics of the Faroe Islands</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Greenland" title="Politics of Greenland">Politics of Greenland</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tmulti tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;max-width:302px"> 
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:153px;max-width:153px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Drottning_Margrethe_av_Danmark_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Drottning_Margrethe_av_Danmark_crop.jpg/151px-Drottning_Margrethe_av_Danmark_crop.jpg" width="151" height="197" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Drottning_Margrethe_av_Danmark_crop.jpg/227px-Drottning_Margrethe_av_Danmark_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Drottning_Margrethe_av_Danmark_crop.jpg/302px-Drottning_Margrethe_av_Danmark_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2577" data-file-height="3369"></a>
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">
         <a href="/wiki/Margrethe_II_of_Denmark" title="Margrethe II of Denmark">Margrethe II</a>,
         <br> 
         <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Denmark" title="Monarchy of Denmark">Queen</a> since 1972
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:145px;max-width:145px"> 
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Lars_L%C3%B8kke_Rasmussen_(2009).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Lars_L%C3%B8kke_Rasmussen_%282009%29.jpg/143px-Lars_L%C3%B8kke_Rasmussen_%282009%29.jpg" width="143" height="197" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Lars_L%C3%B8kke_Rasmussen_%282009%29.jpg/215px-Lars_L%C3%B8kke_Rasmussen_%282009%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Lars_L%C3%B8kke_Rasmussen_%282009%29.jpg/286px-Lars_L%C3%B8kke_Rasmussen_%282009%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2750"></a>
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">
         <a href="/wiki/Lars_L%C3%B8kke_Rasmussen" title="Lars Løkke Rasmussen">Lars Løkke Rasmussen</a>,
         <br> 
         <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Denmark" title="Prime Minister of Denmark">Prime Minister</a> since 2015
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <div style="clear:left"></div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Kingdom of Denmark is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>, in which <a href="/wiki/Margrethe_II_of_Denmark" title="Margrethe II of Denmark">Queen Margrethe II</a> is the head of state. The monarch officially retains <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive power</a> and presides over the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Council_of_State" title="Danish Council of State">Council of State</a> (<a href="/wiki/Privy_council" title="Privy council">privy council</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[68]</a></sup> However, following the introduction of a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a> of government, the duties of the monarch have since become strictly representative and <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial" title="Ceremonial" class="mw-redirect">ceremonial</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[69]</a></sup> such as the formal appointment and dismissal of the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Denmark" title="Prime Minister of Denmark">Prime Minister</a> and other Government ministers. The monarch is not answerable for his or her actions, and the monarch's person is sacrosanct.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[70]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Danish political system operates under a framework laid out in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Denmark" title="Constitution of Denmark">Constitution of Denmark</a>. Changes to it require an absolute majority in two consecutive parliamentary terms and majority approval through a referendum.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[N 10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[71]</a></sup> It has been revised four times, <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Denmark#Changes" title="Constitution of Denmark">most recently</a> in 1953. Denmark has adopted the "<a href="/wiki/Nordic_Model" title="Nordic Model" class="mw-redirect">Nordic model</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Social_Democracy" title="Social Democracy" class="mw-redirect">social democracy</a> as a political ideology, alongside countries like <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> (to an extent).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a>, while acknowledging that democracy is difficult to measure, listed Denmark 5th on its <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">index of democracy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Democracy_Index_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Democracy_Index-19">[10]</a></sup> Denmark also ranks 1st on the <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a>, for government transparency and lack of corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-Burnett_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burnett-82">[72]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Folketing" title="Folketing">Folketing</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Denmark" title="Cabinet of Denmark">Cabinet of Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Det_danske_parlament.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Det_danske_parlament.jpg/220px-Det_danske_parlament.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Det_danske_parlament.jpg/330px-Det_danske_parlament.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Det_danske_parlament.jpg/440px-Det_danske_parlament.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1379" data-file-height="920"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Det_danske_parlament.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The debating chamber of the national parliament, the Folketing.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Danish Parliament is called the Folketing (<a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>: <span lang="da"><i>Folketinget</i></span>). It is the <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislature</a> of the Kingdom of Denmark, passing <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Parliament" title="Act of Parliament">Acts</a> that apply in Denmark and, in limited cases, Greenland and the Faroe Islands. The Folketing is also responsible for adopting the <a href="/wiki/Government_budget" title="Government budget">state's budgets</a>, approving the state's accounts, appointing and exercising control of the Government, and taking part in international cooperation. <a href="/wiki/Bill_(proposed_law)" title="Bill (proposed law)" class="mw-redirect">Bills</a> may be initiated by the Government or by <a href="/wiki/Member_of_parliament" title="Member of parliament">members of parliament</a>. All bills passed must be presented before the Council of State to receive <a href="/wiki/Royal_Assent" title="Royal Assent" class="mw-redirect">Royal Assent</a> within thirty days in order to become law.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[73]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Denmark is a <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a> with <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a>. Membership of the Folketing is based on <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a> of political parties,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[74]</a></sup> with a 2% electoral threshold. Danes elect 175 members to the Folketing, with Greenland and the Faroe Islands electing an additional two members each—179 members in total.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[75]</a></sup> Parliamentary elections are held at least every four years, but it is within the powers of the Prime Minister to ask the monarch to call for an election before the term has elapsed. On a <a href="/wiki/Motion_of_no_confidence" title="Motion of no confidence">vote of no confidence</a>, the Folketing may force a single minister or the entire government to resign.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[76]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:ChrBorg-facade-nov-2012.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/ChrBorg-facade-nov-2012.JPG/220px-ChrBorg-facade-nov-2012.JPG" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/ChrBorg-facade-nov-2012.JPG/330px-ChrBorg-facade-nov-2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/ChrBorg-facade-nov-2012.JPG/440px-ChrBorg-facade-nov-2012.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3643" data-file-height="2485"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:ChrBorg-facade-nov-2012.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Christiansborg_Palace" title="Christiansborg Palace">Christiansborg Palace</a> houses the Folketing, the 
        <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Denmark" title="Supreme Court of Denmark">Supreme Court</a>, and Government offices.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Government of Denmark operates as a <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">cabinet government</a>, where executive authority is exercised—formally on behalf of the monarch—by the Prime Minister and other <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_minister" title="Cabinet minister" class="mw-redirect">cabinet ministers</a>, who head <a href="/wiki/List_of_Danish_government_ministries" title="List of Danish government ministries">ministries</a>. As the executive branch, the Cabinet is responsible for proposing bills and a budget, executing the laws, and guiding the foreign and internal policies of Denmark. The position of prime minister belongs to the person most likely to command the <a href="/wiki/Confidence_and_supply" title="Confidence and supply">confidence</a> of a majority in the Folketing; this is usually the current leader of the largest <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">political party</a> or, more effectively, through a <a href="/wiki/Political_alliance" title="Political alliance">coalition of parties</a>. A single party generally does not have sufficient political power in terms of the number of seats to form a cabinet on its own; Denmark has often been ruled by <a href="/wiki/Coalition_governments" title="Coalition governments" class="mw-redirect">coalition governments</a>, themselves sometimes <a href="/wiki/Minority_government" title="Minority government">minority governments</a> dependent on non-government parties.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[77]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Following a <a href="/wiki/Danish_general_election,_2015" title="Danish general election, 2015">general election defeat</a>, in June 2015 <a href="/wiki/Helle_Thorning-Schmidt" title="Helle Thorning-Schmidt">Helle Thorning-Schmidt</a>, leader of the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democrats_(Denmark)" title="Social Democrats (Denmark)">Social Democrats</a> (<i><span lang="da">Socialdemokraterne</span></i>), resigned as Prime Minister. She was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Lars_L%C3%B8kke_Rasmussen" title="Lars Løkke Rasmussen">Lars Løkke Rasmussen</a>, the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Venstre_(Denmark)" title="Venstre (Denmark)">Liberal Party</a> (<i><span lang="da">Venstre</span></i>). Rasmussen heads <a href="/wiki/Lars_L%C3%B8kke_Rasmussen_II_Cabinet" title="Lars Løkke Rasmussen II Cabinet">a cabinet</a> which, unusually, consists entirely of ministers from his own party.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_judicial_system">Law and judicial system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Law and judicial system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Denmark" title="Law of Denmark">Law of Denmark</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Courts_of_Denmark" title="Courts of Denmark">Courts of Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Denmark" title="Crime in Denmark">Crime in Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Denmark has a <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> system with some references to <a href="/wiki/Germanic_law" title="Germanic law" class="mw-redirect">Germanic law</a>. Denmark resembles Norway and Sweden in never having developed a <a href="/wiki/Case-law" title="Case-law" class="mw-redirect">case-law</a> like that of <a href="/wiki/English_law" title="English law">England</a> and the United States nor comprehensive <a href="/wiki/Code_(law)" title="Code (law)">codes</a> like those of France and Germany. Much of its law is <a href="/wiki/Custom_(law)" title="Custom (law)">customary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[78]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The judicial system of Denmark is divided between courts with regular civil and <a href="/wiki/Criminal_law" title="Criminal law">criminal</a> jurisdiction and administrative courts with jurisdiction over litigation between individuals and the public administration. Articles sixty-two and sixty-four of the Constitution ensure <a href="/wiki/Judicial_independence" title="Judicial independence">judicial independence</a> from government and Parliament by providing that judges shall only be guided by the law, including acts, statutes and practice.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[79]</a></sup> The Kingdom of Denmark does not have a single unified judicial system – Denmark has one system, Greenland another, and the Faroe Islands a third.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[80]</a></sup> However, decisions by the highest courts in Greenland and the Faroe Islands may be appealed to the Danish High Courts. The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Denmark" title="Supreme Court of Denmark">Danish Supreme Court</a> is the highest civil and criminal court responsible for the administration of justice in the Kingdom.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Denmark" title="Foreign relations of Denmark">Foreign relations of Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The foreign policy of Denmark is substantially influenced by <a href="/wiki/Denmark_and_the_European_Union" title="Denmark and the European Union">its membership</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU); Denmark joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC), the EU's predecessor, in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[N 11]</a></sup> Denmark held the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_the_Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Presidency of the Council of the European Union">Presidency of the Council of the European Union</a> on seven occasions, most recently from January to June 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[81]</a></sup> Following <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Denmark ended its two-hundred-year-long policy of <a href="/wiki/Country_neutrality_(international_relations)" title="Country neutrality (international relations)">neutrality</a>. It has been a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">North Atlantic Treaty Organization</a> (NATO) since 1949, and membership remains highly popular.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[82]</a></sup> In recent years, Greenland and the Faroe Islands have been guaranteed a say in foreign policy issues such as fishing, <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whaling</a>, and geopolitical concerns.</p> 
     <p>As a member of <a href="/wiki/Development_Assistance_Committee" title="Development Assistance Committee">Development Assistance Committee</a> (DAC), Denmark has for a long time been among the countries of the world, contributing the largest percentage of gross national income to <a href="/wiki/Development_aid" title="Development aid">development aid</a>. In 2013, Denmark contributed 0.85% of GNI to <a href="/wiki/Aid" title="Aid">foreign aid</a> and was one of only five countries meeting the longstanding UN target for an ODA/GNI ratio of 0.7%. The country participates in both bilateral and multilateral aid, with the aid usually administered by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_of_Denmark" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs of Denmark" class="mw-redirect">Ministry of Foreign Affairs of Denmark</a>. The organizational name of <a href="/wiki/DANIDA" title="DANIDA" class="mw-redirect">DANIDA</a> is often used, in particular when operating bilateral aid.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Denmark" title="Military history of Denmark">Military history of Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Danish_Military_Police.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Danish_Military_Police.JPG/220px-Danish_Military_Police.JPG" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Danish_Military_Police.JPG/330px-Danish_Military_Police.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Danish_Military_Police.JPG/440px-Danish_Military_Police.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2706" data-file-height="1734"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Danish_Military_Police.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Danish MP-soldiers conducting advanced law enforcement training.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Denmark's <a href="/wiki/Armed_forces" title="Armed forces">armed forces</a> are known as the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Defence" title="Danish Defence">Danish Defence</a> (<a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>: <span lang="da"><i>Forsvaret</i></span>). The monarch is <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the Danish Defence, and serves as chief <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomatic</a> official abroad. During peacetime, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Denmark)" title="Ministry of Defence (Denmark)">Ministry of Defence</a> employs around 33,000 in total. The main military branches employ almost 27,000: 15,460 in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Danish_Army" title="Royal Danish Army">Royal Danish Army</a>, 5,300 in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Danish_Navy" title="Royal Danish Navy">Royal Danish Navy</a> and 6,050 in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Danish_Air_Force" title="Royal Danish Air Force">Royal Danish Air Force</a> (all including conscripts).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Danish_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Danish Emergency Management Agency">Danish Emergency Management Agency</a> employs 2,000 (including conscripts), and about 4,000 are in non-branch-specific services like the <a href="/wiki/Defence_Command_(Denmark)" title="Defence Command (Denmark)">Danish Defence Command</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Defence_Intelligence_Service" title="Danish Defence Intelligence Service">Danish Defence Intelligence Service</a>. Furthermore, around 55,000 serve as volunteers in the <a href="/wiki/Home_Guard_(Denmark)" title="Home Guard (Denmark)">Danish Home Guard</a>.</p> 
     <p>Denmark is a long-time supporter of international <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a>, but since the <a href="/wiki/NATO_bombing_of_Yugoslavia" title="NATO bombing of Yugoslavia">NATO bombing of Yugoslavia</a> in 1999 and the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%9314)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–14)">War in Afghanistan</a> in 2001, Denmark has also found a new role as a warring nation, participating actively in several wars and invasions. This relatively new situation has stirred some internal critique, but the Danish population has generally been very supportive, in particular of the War in Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[84]</a></sup> The Danish Defence has around 1,400<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[85]</a></sup> staff in international missions, not including standing contributions to <a href="/wiki/Standing_NRF_Mine_Countermeasures_Group_1" title="Standing NRF Mine Countermeasures Group 1" class="mw-redirect">NATO SNMCMG1</a>. Danish forces were heavily engaged in the former Yugoslavia in the UN Protection Force (<a href="/wiki/UNPROFOR" title="UNPROFOR" class="mw-redirect">UNPROFOR</a>), with <a href="/wiki/IFOR" title="IFOR" class="mw-redirect">IFOR</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[86]</a></sup> and now <a href="/wiki/SFOR" title="SFOR">SFOR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[87]</a></sup> Between 2003 and 2007, there were approximately 450 Danish soldiers in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[88]</a></sup> Denmark also strongly supported <a href="/wiki/Operation_Enduring_Freedom" title="Operation Enduring Freedom">American operations</a> in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> and has contributed both monetarily and materially to the <a href="/wiki/International_Security_Assistance_Force" title="International Security Assistance Force">ISAF</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[89]</a></sup> These initiatives are often described by the authorities as part of a new "active foreign policy" of Denmark.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      Further information: 
      <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Denmark" title="Economy of Denmark">Economy of Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Lego_Color_Bricks.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Lego_Color_Bricks.jpg/220px-Lego_Color_Bricks.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Lego_Color_Bricks.jpg/330px-Lego_Color_Bricks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Lego_Color_Bricks.jpg/440px-Lego_Color_Bricks.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Lego_Color_Bricks.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Lego" title="Lego">Lego</a> bricks are produced by 
        <a href="/wiki/The_Lego_Group" title="The Lego Group">The Lego Group</a>, headquartered in 
        <a href="/wiki/Billund,_Denmark" title="Billund, Denmark">Billund</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Denmark has a <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">high-income</a> <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[90]</a></sup> A liberalisation of import tariffs in 1797 marked the end of <a href="/wiki/Mercantilism" title="Mercantilism">mercantilism</a> and further liberalisation in the 19th and the beginning of the 20th century established the Danish liberal tradition in international trade that was only to be broken by the 1930s.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[91]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Property_rights" title="Property rights" class="mw-redirect">Property rights</a> have enjoyed strong protection. Denmark's economy stands out as one of the most free in the <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">Index of Economic Freedom</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Freedom_of_the_World" title="Economic Freedom of the World">Economic Freedom of the World</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2011-09-20_fraserinstitute_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011-09-20_fraserinstitute-104">[93]</a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Denmark ranks 18th in the world in terms of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">GDP (PPP) per capita</a> and 6th in <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">nominal GDP per capita</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[95]</a></sup> It is the 13th most competitive economy in the world, and 8th in Europe, according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a> in its <i>Global Competitiveness Report 2014–2015</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-wefcomp_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wefcomp-107">[96]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Denmark has the fourth highest ratio of <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_education" title="Tertiary education">tertiary degree</a> holders in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[97]</a></sup> The country ranks highest in the world for <a href="/wiki/Labor_rights" title="Labor rights">workers' rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[98]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_hour_worked" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per hour worked">GDP per hour worked</a> was the 13th highest in 2009. The country has a market income inequality close to the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD" class="mw-redirect">OECD</a> average,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[100]</a></sup> but after public cash transfers the income inequality is <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_income_equality" title="List of countries by income equality">very low</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, Denmark has <a href="/wiki/List_of_minimum_wages_by_country" title="List of minimum wages by country">the world's highest minimum wage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[101]</a></sup> As Denmark has no minimum wage legislation, the high wage floor has been attributed to the power of <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade unions</a>. For example, as the result of a collective bargaining agreement between the <a href="/wiki/Fagligt_F%C3%A6lles_Forbund" title="Fagligt Fælles Forbund">3F trade union</a> and the employers group <a href="/w/index.php?title=Horesta&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Horesta (page does not exist)">Horesta</a>, workers at <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Fast_food_chain" title="Fast food chain" class="mw-redirect">fast food chains</a> make the equivalent of <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>20 an hour, which is more than double what their counterparts earn in the United States, and have access to five weeks' paid vacation, <a href="/wiki/Parental_leave" title="Parental leave">parental leave</a> and a pension plan.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[102]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:EU_Single_Market.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/EU_Single_Market.svg/220px-EU_Single_Market.svg.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/EU_Single_Market.svg/330px-EU_Single_Market.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/EU_Single_Market.svg/440px-EU_Single_Market.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="1300"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:EU_Single_Market.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Denmark is part of the 
        <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>'s 
        <a href="/wiki/Internal_market" title="Internal market">internal market</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>As a result of its acclaimed "<a href="/wiki/Flexicurity" title="Flexicurity">flexicurity</a>" model, Denmark has the most free <a href="/wiki/Labour_economics" title="Labour economics">labour market</a> in Europe, according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>. Employers can hire and fire whenever they want (flexibility), and between jobs, <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a> compensation is very high (security).<sup id="cite_ref-investindk_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investindk-114">[103]</a></sup> Establishing a business can be done in a matter of hours and at very low costs.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[104]</a></sup> No restrictions apply regarding overtime work, which allows companies to operate 24 hours a day, 365 days a year.<sup id="cite_ref-investindk_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investindk-114">[103]</a></sup> Denmark has a competitive <a href="/wiki/Corporate_tax" title="Corporate tax">company tax</a> rate of 24.5% and a special time-limited tax regime for expatriates.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[105]</a></sup> The Danish taxation system is broad based, with a 25% <a href="/wiki/VAT" title="VAT" class="mw-redirect">VAT</a>, in addition to excise taxes, income taxes and other fees. The overall level of taxation (sum of all taxes, as a percentage of GDP) is estimated to be 46% in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[106]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Denmark's currency, the <i><a href="/wiki/Danish_krone" title="Danish krone">krone</a></i> (DKK), is <a href="/wiki/Fixed_exchange_rate" title="Fixed exchange rate" class="mw-redirect">pegged</a> at approximately 7.46 kroner per euro through the <a href="/wiki/European_Exchange_Rate_Mechanism" title="European Exchange Rate Mechanism">ERM</a>. Although a <a href="/wiki/Danish_euro_referendum,_2000" title="Danish euro referendum, 2000">September 2000 referendum</a> rejected adopting the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a><sup id="cite_ref-denmarkandtheeuro_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-denmarkandtheeuro-118">[107]</a></sup>– and entering the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> – the country in practice follows the policies set forth in the <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_Monetary_Union_of_the_European_Union" title="Economic and Monetary Union of the European Union">Economic and Monetary Union of the European Union</a> and meets the economic <a href="/wiki/Euro_convergence_criteria" title="Euro convergence criteria">convergence criteria</a> needed to adopt the euro. The majority of the political parties in the Folketing support adopting the euro, but as yet a new referendum has not been held, despite plans;<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[108]</a></sup> scepticism of the EU among Danish voters has historically been strong.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/StatBank" title="StatBank">StatBank</a> is the name of a large <a href="/wiki/Statistical_database" title="Statistical database">statistical database</a> maintained by the central authority of statistics in Denmark. Online distribution of statistics has been a part of the dissemination strategy in Denmark since 1985.</p> 
     <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry_and_exports">Industry and exports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Industry and exports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Fishing_industry_in_Denmark" title="Fishing industry in Denmark">Fishing industry in Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Sow_with_piglet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Sow_with_piglet.jpg/220px-Sow_with_piglet.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Sow_with_piglet.jpg/330px-Sow_with_piglet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Sow_with_piglet.jpg/440px-Sow_with_piglet.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="1674"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Sow_with_piglet.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Denmark is a leading producer of 
        <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">pork</a>, and the largest exporter of pork products in the EU.
        <sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[109]</a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Once a predominantly <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agricultural</a> country on account of its <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable</a> landscape, since 1945 Denmark has greatly expanded its <a href="/wiki/Industrial_base" title="Industrial base" class="mw-redirect">industrial base</a> so that by 2006 industry contributed about 25% of GDP and agriculture less than 2%.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[110]</a></sup> Support for <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a> is high – in a 2007 poll 76% responded that globalisation is a good thing.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[111]</a></sup> 70% of trade flows are inside the European Union. As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Denmark has the 10th highest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_exports_per_capita" title="List of countries by exports per capita">export per capita in the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-63">[54]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Denmark's major industries include <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemicals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">food processing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding" title="Shipbuilding">shipbuilding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry" title="Pharmaceutical industry">pharmaceuticals</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Construction" title="Construction">construction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-63">[54]</a></sup> The country's main exports are: industrial production/manufactured goods 73.3% (of which machinery and instruments were 21.4%, and fuels (oil, natural gas), chemicals, etc. 26%); agricultural products and others for consumption 18.7% (in 2009 meat and meat products were 5.5% of total export; fish and fish products 2.9%).<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_63-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-63">[54]</a></sup> Denmark is a net exporter of food and energy and has for a number of years had a <a href="/wiki/Balance_of_payments" title="Balance of payments">balance of payments</a> surplus while battling an equivalent of approximately 39% of GNP <a href="/wiki/External_debt" title="External debt">foreign debt</a> or more than <a href="/wiki/Danish_krone" title="Danish krone">DKK</a> 300&nbsp;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[112]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2013, the 20 largest companies by turnover were <a href="/wiki/A.P._M%C3%B8ller-M%C3%A6rsk" title="A.P. Møller-Mærsk" class="mw-redirect">A.P. Møller-Mærsk</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wrist_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wrist Group (page does not exist)">Wrist Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/ISS_A/S" title="ISS A/S">ISS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Novo_Nordisk" title="Novo Nordisk">Novo Nordisk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlsberg_Group" title="Carlsberg Group">Carlsberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/DONG_Energy" title="DONG Energy">DONG Energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arla_Foods" title="Arla Foods">Arla Foods</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Shipping_%26_Trading_Company" title="United Shipping &amp; Trading Company">United Shipping &amp; Trading Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danish_Crown_AmbA" title="Danish Crown AmbA">Danish Crown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dansk_Supermarked" title="Dansk Supermarked">Dansk Supermarked</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vestas_Wind_Systems" title="Vestas Wind Systems" class="mw-redirect">Vestas Wind Systems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dansk_Landbrugs_Grovvareselskab" title="Dansk Landbrugs Grovvareselskab">DLG</a>, <a href="/wiki/DSV_(company)" title="DSV (company)">DSV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coop_Danmark" title="Coop Danmark" class="mw-redirect">Coop Danmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danfoss" title="Danfoss">Danfoss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Statoil" title="Statoil">Statoil Refining Danmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/SAS_Group" title="SAS Group">SAS Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Tobacco_Group" title="Scandinavian Tobacco Group">Skandinavisk Holding</a>, <a href="/wiki/TDC_A/S" title="TDC A/S">TDC</a>, and <a href="/wiki/FLSmidth" title="FLSmidth">FLSmidth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[113]</a></sup> Smaller notable companies include <a href="/wiki/Grundfos" title="Grundfos">Grundfos</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Lego_Group" title="The Lego Group">The Lego Group</a>.</p> 
     <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Denmark" title="Energy in Denmark">Energy in Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:DanishWindTurbines.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/DanishWindTurbines.jpg/220px-DanishWindTurbines.jpg" width="220" height="77" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/DanishWindTurbines.jpg/330px-DanishWindTurbines.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/DanishWindTurbines.jpg/440px-DanishWindTurbines.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="279"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:DanishWindTurbines.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Middelgrunden" title="Middelgrunden">Middelgrunden</a>, an offshore wind farm near Copenhagen.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Denmark has considerably large deposits of oil and natural gas in the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> and ranks as number 32 in the world among net exporters of <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">crude oil</a><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[114]</a></sup> and was producing 259,980 barrels of crude oil a day in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[115]</a></sup> Denmark is a long-time leader in <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a>: In 2015 <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">wind turbines</a> provided 42,1% of the total power consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[116]</a></sup> in May 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Denmark derived 3.1% of its gross domestic product from renewable (clean) energy technology and energy efficiency, or around €6.5&nbsp;billion ($9.4&nbsp;billion).<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[117]</a></sup> Denmark is connected by <a href="/wiki/Electric_transmission_lines" title="Electric transmission lines" class="mw-redirect">electric transmission lines</a> to other European countries. On 6 September 2012, Denmark launched the biggest wind turbine in the world, and will add four more over the next four years.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Electricity_sector_in_Denmark" title="Electricity sector in Denmark">Denmark's electricity sector</a> has integrated energy sources such as wind power into the national grid. Denmark now aims to focus on intelligent battery systems (<a href="/wiki/Vehicle-to-grid" title="Vehicle-to-grid">V2G</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">plug-in vehicles</a> in the transport sector.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[118]</a></sup> The country is a member nation of the <a href="/wiki/International_Renewable_Energy_Agency" title="International Renewable Energy Agency">International Renewable Energy Agency</a> (IRENA).<sup id="cite_ref-IRENAstates_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRENAstates-130">[119]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Denmark" title="Transport in Denmark">Transport in Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Significant investment has been made in building road and rail links between regions in Denmark, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Great_Belt_Fixed_Link" title="Great Belt Fixed Link">Great Belt Fixed Link</a>, which connects <a href="/wiki/Zealand" title="Zealand">Zealand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Funen" title="Funen">Funen</a>. It is now possible to drive from <a href="/wiki/Frederikshavn" title="Frederikshavn">Frederikshavn</a> in northern <a href="/wiki/Jutland" title="Jutland">Jutland</a> to <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> on eastern Zealand without leaving the motorway. The main railway operator is <a href="/wiki/DSB_(railway_company)" title="DSB (railway company)">DSB</a> for passenger services and <a href="/wiki/DB_Schenker_Rail" title="DB Schenker Rail">DB Schenker Rail</a> for freight trains. The railway tracks are maintained by <a href="/wiki/Banedanmark" title="Banedanmark">Banedanmark</a>. The North Sea and the Baltic Sea are intertwined by various, international ferry links. Construction of the <a href="/wiki/Fehmarn_Belt_Fixed_Link" title="Fehmarn Belt Fixed Link">Fehmarn Belt Fixed Link</a>, connecting Denmark and Germany with a second link, will start in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[120]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Copenhagen has a <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">rapid transit</a> system, the <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Metro" title="Copenhagen Metro">Copenhagen Metro</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Copenhagen" title="Greater Copenhagen" class="mw-redirect">Greater Copenhagen</a> area has an extensive electrified suburban railway network, the <a href="/wiki/S-train" title="S-train">S-train</a>. In the four biggest cities - <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aarhus" title="Aarhus">Aarhus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Odense" title="Odense">Odense</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aalborg" title="Aalborg">Aalborg</a> - light rail systems are planned to be in operation around 2020. The light rail in Greater Copenhagen will traverse 11 municipalities, providing a much needed corridor from <a href="/wiki/Lyngby" title="Lyngby" class="mw-redirect">Lyngby</a> in the north to <a href="/wiki/Ish%C3%B8j" title="Ishøj">Ishøj</a> in the south .<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[121]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Copenhagen_Airport_Mai_2009_PD_131.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Copenhagen_Airport_Mai_2009_PD_131.JPG/220px-Copenhagen_Airport_Mai_2009_PD_131.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Copenhagen_Airport_Mai_2009_PD_131.JPG/330px-Copenhagen_Airport_Mai_2009_PD_131.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Copenhagen_Airport_Mai_2009_PD_131.JPG/440px-Copenhagen_Airport_Mai_2009_PD_131.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Copenhagen_Airport_Mai_2009_PD_131.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Airport" title="Copenhagen Airport">Copenhagen Airport</a> is the largest airport in Scandinavia and 
        <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">15th-busiest in Europe</a>.
        <sup id="cite_ref-cph_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cph-133">[122]</a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>With Norway and Sweden, Denmark is part of the <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a>. <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Airport" title="Copenhagen Airport">Copenhagen Airport</a> is Scandinavia's busiest passenger airport, handling over 25 million passengers in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-cph_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cph-133">[122]</a></sup> Other notable airports are <a href="/wiki/Billund_Airport" title="Billund Airport">Billund Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aalborg_Airport" title="Aalborg Airport">Aalborg Airport</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aarhus_Airport" title="Aarhus Airport">Aarhus Airport</a>.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Cycling_in_Denmark" title="Cycling in Denmark">Cycling in Denmark</a> is a common form of transport, particularly for the young and for city dwellers. With a network of bicycle routes extending more than 12,000&nbsp;km<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[123]</a></sup> and an estimated 7,000&nbsp;km<sup id="cite_ref-vcta_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vcta-135">[124]</a></sup> of <a href="/wiki/Segregated_cycle_facilities" title="Segregated cycle facilities" class="mw-redirect">segregated dedicated bicycle paths and lanes</a>, Denmark has a solid <a href="/wiki/Cycling_infrastructure" title="Cycling infrastructure">bicycle infrastructure</a>.</p> 
     <p>Private vehicles are increasingly used as a means of transport. Because of the <a href="/wiki/Car_taxation" title="Car taxation" class="mw-redirect">high registration tax</a> (180%), <a href="/wiki/VAT" title="VAT" class="mw-redirect">VAT</a> (25%), and one of the world's highest income tax rates, new cars are very expensive. The purpose of the tax is to discourage car ownership. In 2007, an attempt was made by the government to favour environmentally friendly cars by slightly reducing taxes on high mileage vehicles. However, this has had little effect, and in 2008 Denmark experienced an increase in the import of fuel inefficient old cars,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[125]</a></sup> as the cost for older cars—including taxes—keeps them within the budget of many Danes. As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the average car age is 9.2 years.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[126]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Internet_in_Denmark" title="Internet in Denmark">Internet in Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <p>In the 20th century, Danes have also been innovative in several fields of the technology sector. Danish companies have been influential in the shipping industry with the design of the largest and most energy efficient container ships in the world, the <a href="/wiki/Maersk_Triple_E_class" title="Maersk Triple E class">Maersk Triple E class</a>, and Danish engineers have contributed to the design of <a href="/wiki/MAN_Diesel" title="MAN Diesel">MAN Diesel</a> engines. In the software and electronic field, Denmark contributed to design and manufacturing of <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Mobile_Telephone" title="Nordic Mobile Telephone">Nordic Mobile Telephones</a>, and the now-defunct Danish company <a href="/w/index.php?title=DanCall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="DanCall (page does not exist)">DanCall</a> was among the first to develop <a href="/wiki/GSM" title="GSM">GSM</a> mobile phones.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[127]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Danish engineers are world-leading in providing diabetes care equipment and medication products from <a href="/wiki/Novo_Nordisk" title="Novo Nordisk">Novo Nordisk</a> and, since 2000, the Danish <a href="/wiki/Biotech" title="Biotech" class="mw-redirect">biotech</a> company <a href="/wiki/Novozymes" title="Novozymes">Novozymes</a>, the world market leader in enzymes for first generation starch based bioethanol, has pioneered development of enzymes for converting waste to <a href="/wiki/Cellulosic_ethanol" title="Cellulosic ethanol">cellulosic ethanol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[128]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Medicon_Valley" title="Medicon Valley">Medicon Valley</a></i>, spanning the <a href="/wiki/%C3%98resund_Region" title="Øresund Region">Øresund Region</a> between Zealand and Sweden, is one of Europe's largest <a href="/wiki/Life_science" title="Life science" class="mw-redirect">life science</a> clusters, containing a large number of life science companies and research institutions located within a very small geographical area. Danish-born software engineers have taken leading roles in some of the world's programming languages: <a href="/wiki/Anders_Hejlsberg" title="Anders Hejlsberg">Anders Hejlsberg</a>, (<a href="/wiki/Turbo_Pascal" title="Turbo Pascal">Turbo Pascal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Embarcadero_Delphi" title="Embarcadero Delphi" class="mw-redirect">Delphi</a>, <a href="/wiki/C_Sharp_(programming_language)" title="C Sharp (programming language)">C#</a>); <a href="/wiki/Rasmus_Lerdorf" title="Rasmus Lerdorf">Rasmus Lerdorf</a>, (<a href="/wiki/PHP" title="PHP">PHP</a>); <a href="/wiki/Bjarne_Stroustrup" title="Bjarne Stroustrup">Bjarne Stroustrup</a>, (<a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a>); <a href="/wiki/David_Heinemeier_Hansson" title="David Heinemeier Hansson">David Heinemeier Hansson</a>, (<a href="/wiki/Ruby_on_Rails" title="Ruby on Rails">Ruby on Rails</a>); <a href="/wiki/Lars_Bak_(computer_programmer)" title="Lars Bak (computer programmer)">Lars Bak</a>, a pioneer in virtual machines (<a href="/wiki/V8_(JavaScript_engine)" title="V8 (JavaScript engine)">V8</a>, <a href="/wiki/Java_virtual_machine" title="Java virtual machine">Java VM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dart_(programming_language)" title="Dart (programming language)">Dart</a>). Physicist <a href="/wiki/Lene_Vestergaard_Hau" title="Lene Vestergaard Hau" class="mw-redirect">Lene Vestergaard Hau</a> is the first person to stop light, leading to advances in <a href="/wiki/Quantum_computing" title="Quantum computing">quantum computing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanoscale_engineering" title="Nanoscale engineering" class="mw-redirect">nanoscale engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linear_optics" title="Linear optics" class="mw-redirect">linear optics</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_policy">Public policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Public policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Flexicurity" title="Flexicurity">Flexicurity</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Taxation_in_Denmark" title="Taxation in Denmark">Taxation in Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Denmark_Confirms_Participation_in_E-ELT.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Denmark_Confirms_Participation_in_E-ELT.jpg/220px-Denmark_Confirms_Participation_in_E-ELT.jpg" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Denmark_Confirms_Participation_in_E-ELT.jpg/330px-Denmark_Confirms_Participation_in_E-ELT.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Denmark_Confirms_Participation_in_E-ELT.jpg/440px-Denmark_Confirms_Participation_in_E-ELT.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2779" data-file-height="2210"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Denmark_Confirms_Participation_in_E-ELT.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> With an investment of 8.5 million euros over the ten-year construction period, Denmark confirms participation in 
        <a href="/wiki/E-ELT" title="E-ELT" class="mw-redirect">E-ELT</a>.
        <sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[129]</a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>After <a href="/wiki/Deregulation" title="Deregulation">deregulating</a> the labour market in the 1990s, Denmark has one of the most free labour markets among the European countries. According to <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> labour market rankings, the <a href="/wiki/Labour_market_flexibility" title="Labour market flexibility">labour market flexibility</a> is at the same levels as the United States. The model is called "Flexicurity". Denmark is also characterized by the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_model" title="Nordic model">Nordic model</a>. The largest taxes are 25% <a href="/wiki/Value-added_tax" title="Value-added tax">value-added tax</a> and <a href="/wiki/Personal_income_tax" title="Personal income tax" class="mw-redirect">personal income tax</a> (minimum tax rate for adults is 42% scaling to over 60%).<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[130]</a></sup> Other taxes include the registration tax on private vehicles, at a rate of 180%, on top of VAT. In July 2007, this was changed slightly in an attempt to favour more <a href="/wiki/Fuel_efficiency" title="Fuel efficiency">fuel efficient</a> cars whilst maintaining the average taxation level.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[131]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 6% of the population was reported to live below the <a href="/wiki/Poverty_line" title="Poverty line" class="mw-redirect">poverty line</a>, when adjusted for taxes and transfers. Denmark has the 2nd lowest relative poverty rate in the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD" class="mw-redirect">OECD</a>, below the 11.3% OECD average.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD1_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD1-143">[132]</a></sup> The share of the population reporting that they feel that they cannot afford to buy sufficient food in Denmark is less than half of the OECD average.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD1_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD1-143">[132]</a></sup> With an employment rate of 72.8%, Denmark ranks 7th highest among the OECD countries, and above the OECD average of 66.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD1_143-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD1-143">[132]</a></sup> The number of unemployed people is forecast to be 65,000 in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-2006forecasts_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2006forecasts-144">[133]</a></sup> The number of people in the <a href="/wiki/Legal_working_age" title="Legal working age">working age</a> group, less disability pensioners etc., will grow by 10,000 to 2,860,000, and jobs by 70,000 to 2,790,000;<sup id="cite_ref-2006forecasts_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2006forecasts-144">[133]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Part-time" title="Part-time" class="mw-redirect">part-time</a> jobs are included.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[134]</a></sup> Because of the present high demand and short supply of skilled labour, for instance for factory and service jobs, including hospital nurses and physicians, the annual average <a href="/wiki/Working_time" title="Working time">working hours</a> have risen, especially compared with the <a href="/wiki/Recession" title="Recession">recession</a> 1987–1993.<sup id="cite_ref-BusinessDK_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BusinessDK-146">[135]</a></sup> Increasingly, service workers of all kinds are in demand, i.e. in the <a href="/wiki/Mail" title="Mail">postal services</a> and as bus drivers, and academics.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[136]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The level of <a href="/wiki/Unemployment_benefits" title="Unemployment benefits">unemployment benefits</a> is dependent on former employment (the maximum benefit is at 90% of the wage) and at times also on membership of an unemployment fund, which is almost always—but need not be—administered by a trade union, and the previous payment of contributions. However, the largest share of the financing is still carried by the central government and is financed by general taxation, and only to a minor degree from earmarked contributions. There is no taxation, however, on proceeds gained from selling one's home (provided there <i>was</i> any <a href="/wiki/Home_equity" title="Home equity">home equity</a> (<span lang="da"><i>friværdi</i></span>)), as the marginal tax rate on capital income from housing savings is around 0%.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[137]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denmark&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Denmark" title="Demographics of Denmark">Demographics of Denmark</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
       <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden"> 
        <p><br></p> 
        <p><br></p> 
        <p><br></p> 
        <p><br></p> 
        <p><br></p> 
        <p><br></p> 
        <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:DarkGray"></div> 
        <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 560.49018062266px; border-left-color:MediumBlue"></div> 
        <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:MediumBlue"></div> 
        <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:MediumBlue"></div> 
        <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 107.70325341692px; border-left-color:DarkBlue"></div> 
        <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DarkBlue"></div> 
        <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DarkBlue"></div> 
        <div style="position:absolute;left:0;top:0">
         <img alt="Circle frame.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Circle_frame.svg/200px-Circle_frame.svg.png" width="200" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Circle_frame.svg/300px-Circle_frame.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Circle_frame.svg/400px-Circle_frame.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="200">
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <p>Population by ancestry (2015)<sup id="cite_ref-Immigration_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Immigration-149">[138]</a></sup></p> 
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;People of Danish origin (88.09%)
        </div> 
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:MediumBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Immigrant (9.1%)
        </div> 
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkGray; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Descendent of an immigrant (2.81%)
        </div> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In July 2015 the population of Denmark was 5.67&nbsp;million people.<sup id="cite_ref-pop1_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop1-7">[3]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Median" title="Median">median</a> age is 41.4 years, with 0.97 males per female. The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> is 1.73 children born per woman; despite the low birth rate, the population is still growing at an average annual rate of 0.22%.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_63-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-63">[54]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Happiness_Report" title="World Happiness Report">World Happiness Report</a> frequently ranks Denmark's population as the happiest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-happiness_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-happiness-150">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Earth_Institute_2013_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Earth_Institute_2013-151">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BruceStokes_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BruceStokes-152">[141]</a></sup> This has been attributed to the country's highly regarded education and <a href="/wiki/Health_care_in_Denmark" title="Health care in Denmark" class="mw-redirect">health care</a> systems,<sup id="cite_ref-Taylor_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor-153">[142]</a></sup> and its low level of <a href="/wiki/Income_inequality" title="Income inequality" class="mw-redirect">income inequality</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eurogini_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurogini-12">[7]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Denmark has been an historically <a href="/wiki/Homogeneity_(statistics)" title="Homogeneity (statistics)">homogeneous</a> nation for centuries. However, as its neighbouring Scandinavian countries, Denmark has recently been transformed from a nation of <a href="/wiki/Net_migration" title="Net migration" class="mw-redirect">net emigration</a>, up until World War II, to a nation of net immigration. Today, <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Denmark" title="Immigration to Denmark">immigration to Denmark</a> consists particularly of <a href="/wiki/Asylum_seeker" title="Asylum seeker" class="mw-redirect">asylum seekers</a> and persons who arrive as family dependants.<sup id="cite_ref-migrants_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-migrants-154">[143]</a></sup> In addition, Denmark annually receives a number of citizens from <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">western countries</a>, notably Nordic countries, the EU, and North America, who seek residency to work or study for a definite period of time. Recently, substantial numbers of workers—several tens of thousands—from the <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">new EU accession countries</a>, especially Poland and the Baltic nations, have arrived to perform menial labour in construction, agriculture, consumer industries, and cleaning.<sup id="cite_ref-migrants_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-migrants-154">[143]</a></sup> Overall, the net migration rate in 2015 was 2.2 migrant(s)/1,000 population, comparable to the United Kingdom and well below other <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">North European</a> countries, except the Baltic states.<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_63-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-63">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[145]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>There are no official statistics on <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic groups</a>, but according to 2015 figures from <a href="/wiki/Statistics_Denmark" title="Statistics Denmark">Statistics Denmark</a>, approximately 88% of Denmark's population of 5,678,348 was of <a href="/wiki/Danes" title="Danes">Danish</a> descent, defined as having at least one parent who was born in Denmark and has Danish citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-Immigration_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Immigration-149">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-denonly_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-denonly-11">[N 5]</a></sup> Much of the remaining 12% were of a foreign background, defined as immigrants or descendants of recent immigrants. With the same definition, the most common countries of origin were <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Turkey" title="Demographics of Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraqis" title="Iraqis">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syrians" title="Syrians" class="mw-redirect">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somalis" title="Somalis">Somalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Iran" title="Demographics of Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Afghanistan" title="Demographics of Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavs" title="Yugoslavs">Yugoslavia</a> and its successor states.<sup id="cite_ref-Immigration_149-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Immigration-149">[138]</a></sup></p>
